Jamison Brereton

35 (269)
Indra
Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
A simple hymn, entirely devoted to IndraтАЩs journey to the sacrifice and his enjoy ment of it, mostly expressed in the imperative. The progress of the hymn is com pletely chronological, from the yoking of his pair of horses, through the journey, during which Indra is exhorted to pass by other sacrificers (vs. 5), and finally the arrival at the ritual ground, properly prepared, and the drinking of the soma. The mention of the Maruts in verses 7 and 9 suggests that the Midday Pressing, devoted to Indra and the Maruts jointly at least in Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra circles, is the sacrifice in ques tion (see also, for example, III.32). There is also a rather charming concern for the welfare of IndraтАЩs horses (vss. 3, 7).
In the context of R╠еgvedic poetry what is striking are the absent elements. There is neither praise of the god honored nor any mention of his attributes or heroic deeds. (The sole exception is 9b, with its unelaborated allusion to the MarutsтАЩ role in strengthening Indra and the alliance resulting therefrom.) Nor do we hear about the purpose of IndraтАЩs soma-drinkingтАФrousing him to perform heroic deeds either in the past or for our benefit now. Nor, despite the many imperatives, does the poet ask for any gifts or for aid of any sort. It is an extraordinarily focused hymn, and its apparent simplicity may result not from artlessness, but from careful pruning.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬStay, Indra, having yoked the horses to the car, as V─Бyu stops when he has put to his steds, and come to our presence; solicited by us to drink of the Soma, which with reverence we offer for your exhilaration.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Mount the pair of fallow bays being yoked to the chariot. Drive, like the wind, to our teams [=poetic thoughts].
You will drink the stalk when you have surged to us. Indra, hail! We have given (it) to you for your exhilaration.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda is somewhat oddly expressed: Indra is urged to mount the horses yoked to the chariot, but not only is horseback riding very rare in the RV, but no one is likely to mount a horse being used to pull a vehicle. This must be an awkwardly expanded version of the usual тАЬmount the chariotтАЭ (see 4c below).

The niy├║t- тАШteamтАЩ is generally associated with, indeed belongs to, V─Бyu, who is regularly called niy├║tvant- тАШpossessing niy├║tsтАЩ. However, the word is sometimes used in a reciprocal value: just as V─Бyu and Indra drive to us with their niy├║ts, so do our niy├║ts, the тАШteamsтАЩ of poetic thoughts, drive in return to the gods, in passages where niy├║t- is parallel to words for тАШthought, hymnтАЩ, etc. Cf., e.g., I.134.2, 135.2, VI.35.3, 47.14, VII.23.4, 90.1, X.26.1. It is therefore not nec., with Bloomfield (RVReps ad loc.) to assume that тАЬniy├║to is for niy├║dbhiс╕е.тАЭ

Griffith

MOUNT the Bay Horses to thy chariot harnessed, and come to us like Vayu with his coursers.
Thou, hastening to us, shalt drink the Soma. Hail, Indra. We have poured it for thy rapture.

Geldner

Besteige das an den Wagen geschirrte Falbenpaar; komm zu uns, wie Vayu die Niyutgespanne besteigend! Im Galopp kommend sollst du bei uns den Trank trinken. Indra! Wohl bekomm┬┤s! Wir haben ihn dir zum Rausche gespendet.

Grassmann

Besteig die F├╝chse, die den Wagen ziehen, komm zu uns wie der Wind mit seinen Rossen, Zu uns hinschiessend trinke dann den Soma, o Indra, Heil! wir spendeten zum Rausch dir.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрддрд╛рдп рдкреБрд░реБрднрд┐рд░реНрдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рд░реНрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреИрд░реНрдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реНрдердорд╛рд╣реВрддрд╛рдп рддреБрднреНрдпрдордЬрд┐рд░рд╛ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдЧрдордирд╢реАрд▓реМ рд╕рдкреНрддреА рд╕рд░реНрдкрдгрд╢реАрддреМ рд╣рд░реА рд╣рд░рд┐рдирд╛рдордХрд╛рд╡рд╢реНрд╡реМ рд░рдерд╕реНрдп рдзреВрд░реНрд╖реБ рдпреБрдЧрдкреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддреЗрд╖реВрдкрд╛ рдпреБрдирдЬреНрдорд┐ ред рдЕрд╣рдВ рддрдерд╛ рдпреЛрдЬрдпрд╛рдорд┐ ред рджреНрд░рд╡рддреН рд╕ рд░рдереЛ рдпрдерд╛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрддреНрддрдереЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рд╕рдореНрднреГрддрдВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрдпрдЬреБрд░реНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рд╕реНрддреЛрдореИрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рд╕рдореНрднрд╛рд░реИрдГ рд╕рдореНрдкреВрд░реНрдгрдорд┐рдордВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореБрдкрд╛ рд╡рд╣рд╛рддрдГ ред рддрд╛рд╡рд╢реНрд╡реМ ред рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧрд╛рд╡рд╣рддрд╛рдореН ред рдзреВрд░реНрд╖реБ ред рдзреБрд░реНрд╡реА рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд░реНрдзрдГ ред рдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреН ред рд░рд╛рд▓реНрд▓реЛрдк рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рдХрд╛рд░рд▓реЛрдкрдГ рд╡реНрд░реЛрд░реБрдкрдзрд╛рдпрд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГ ред рд╕рд╛рд╡реЗрдХрд╛рдЪ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдШрдХреНрддреЗрд░реБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддрд╛ ред рдпреБрдирдЬреНрдорд┐ ред рдпреБрдЬрд┐рд░реН рдпреЛрдЧреЗ ред рд░реБрдзрд╛рджрд┐рдГ ред рд▓рдЯрд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГ ред рджреНрд░рд╡рддреН ред рджреНрд░реБ рдЧрддрд╛рд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реЗ рд▓рдЩрд┐ рд░реБрдкрдореН ред рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрдирд╛рдиреНрддреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рд╡рд╣рд╛рддрдГ ред рд╡рд╣реЗрд░реНрд▓реЗрдЯреНрдпрд╛рдбрд╛рдЧрдореЗ рд░реВрдкрдВ рее реи рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI harness for you, who is invoked by many, the swift gliding horses to the shafts of the car, that they may bear Indra to this sacrifice that is prepared with all (that is required).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The nimble span, the pair of fallow bays I yoke to the yoke-poles of the chariot for the much invoked one.
The two will bring Indra right here to this sacrifice assembled from every side, as if at a run.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The most natural reading of y├бth─Б in c is as a subordinator in a purpose clause (тАШso thatтАЩ) with the subjunctive ─Б╠Бvah─Бtaс╕е in d, and this is how the standard tr.

take it. But there is a major stumbling block: the verb is unaccented. Oldenberg seems willing to emend to an accented verb; Geldner suggests that if the unaccented verb is bothersome, assume an ellipsis in c. I have, in somewhat ad hoc fashion, taken y├бth─Б as a sort of simile marker with drav├бt. I am not entirely satisfied with this solution, but it does more or less fit category 4) in GrassmannтАЩs lemma y├бth─Б, and I am quite reluctant to put an unaccented verb into a subordinate clause. A similar phrase in the next hymn, where y├бth─Б marks a localized comparison, gives support to the interpr. here; see III.36.6 prasav├бс╣З y├бth─Б тАЬlike a shotтАЭ (tr. similarly by all standard tr.).

Griffith

For him, the God who is invoked by many, the two swift Bay Steeds to the pole I harness,
That they in fleet course may bring Indra hither, e’en to this sacrifice arranged completely.

Geldner

Ich schirre dem Vielgerufenen das rasche Gespann, das Falbenpaar an die Joche des Wagens, auf da├Я sie Indra zu diesem vollst├дndig zuger├╝steten Opfer eilig heranfahren.

Die schnellen Rosse schirr ich an, die hellen, dem vielgerufnen Indra an die Deichsel, Dass rasch sie ihn zu diesem Opfer fahren, das wir aus allem recht zusammenf├╝gten.

Elizarenkova

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд▓реЛрдЧ рд╡рд╛рд╣рдиреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдЖрджрд┐ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕рдВрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдЪрд▓рд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рдХрд┐рд╕-рдХрд┐рд╕ рджреЗрд╢ рдХреЛ рди рдЬрд╛ рд╕рдХреИрдВ ? рдФрд░ рдЙрдирдХреЛ рдХреМрдирд╕рд╛ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рд╣реИ рдЬреЛ рди рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрд╡реИ ? реереирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдерд╛рд╜рд╣рдВ рдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рдордВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛рд╡рд╣рд╛рддреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддреЛ рджреНрд░рд╡рддреНрд╕рдореНрднреГрддрдВ рдЪрд┐рджрдкреНрдпреБрдкрд╛рд╡рд╣рд╛рддрд╕реНрддреМ рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрддрд╛рдп рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рд╡рдЬрд┐рд░рд╛ рд╕рдкреНрддреА рд╣рд░реА рд░рдерд╕реНрдп рдзреВрд░реНрд╖реБ рдпреБрдирдЬреНрдорд┐ рддреМ рдпреВрдпрдордкрд┐ рдпреБрдЩреНрдЧреНрдзреНрд╡рдореН реереирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЙрдк) (рдЕрдЬрд┐рд░рд╛) рдпрд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкреНрддрд╛рд░реМ (рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрддрд╛рдп) рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рд░рд╛рд╣реВрддрд╛рдп (рд╕рдкреНрддреА) рд╕рджреНрдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрдкрдиреНрддреМред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реАрддрд┐ рдЧреБрдгреЗ рдХреГрддреЗ рд░реЗрдлрд▓реЛрдкрдГред (рд╣рд░реА) рд╣рд░рдгрд╢реАрд▓реМ (рд░рдерд╕реНрдп) рдпрд╛рдирд╕реНрдп (рдзреВрд░реНрд╖реБ) рд░рдерд╛рдзрд╛рд░рд╛рд╡рдпрд╡реЗрд╖реБ (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рдпреБрдирдЬреНрдорд┐) (рджреНрд░рд╡рддреН) рджреНрд░рд╡рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рддреН (рдпрдерд╛) (рд╕рдореНрднреГрддрдореН) рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧреНрдзреГрддрдореН (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддрдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ (рдЪрд┐рддреН) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рдЙрдк) (рдЗрдордореН) рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдореН (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН) рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдпрдореН (рдЖ) (рд╡рд╣рд╛рддрдГ) рд╡рд╣реЗрддрд╛рдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдореН реереирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShowerer (of benefits), giver of food, guide hither your vigorous horses, defending (us) against foes, and protect (your worshippers); here unharness the bay steeds, and give them fodder, and you eat daily suitable food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Eat suitable food: sadс╣Ы┼Ы─лr addhi dh─Бn─Бс╕е = eat suitable grains, i.e. fried barley, bhс╣Ыс╣гс╣нayav─Бn

Jamison Brereton

Lead near the two bullish (stallions), protecting them from the scorching heat, and help themтАФyou autonomous bull.
Let the two horses graze. Unhitch the two sorrels here. Every day eat roasted grains of the same appearance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Medial nayasva is one of the relatively few middle forms to this pres. stem.

It is presumably used here because Indra is leading his own horses.

The crux in this vs. is the hapax cmpd. tapuс╣гp─Б╠Б-. Grassmann glosses it тАШwarmes trinkendтАЩ, perhaps referring to the gharma drink; in this he is tentatively fld by Mayrhofer (EWA s.v. t├бpuс╣г-). But this -us-stem, t├бpus-, refers only to heat, generally menacing scorching heat, and in any case the horses shouldnтАЩt be drinking the gharma drink (or probably any hot drink at all). The word is discussed by Scarlatta (305-6), who offers several possible interpr. The interpr. is made more difficult by the uncertain grammatical identity of the form. It appears in sandhi as tapuс╣гpс╣Уt├йm, is taken by the Pp. as tapuс╕етАЩp─Б╠Б, and is generally analyzed as a dual, modifying the bullish (horses) – so Geldner, Renou, Scarlatta, Witzel Got┼Н. However, Geldner suggests in n. 3a that the form could represent irregular sandhi for tapuс╣гp─Б(с╕е) ut├б (that is, a double application of sandhi, first losing the final -s before vowel and then coalescing the vowels) and therefore be a nom. sg., modifying Indra. I have adopted this solution; it doesn’t make much sense for the horses themselves to be doing the protecting, but IndraтАЩs protective role would fit with the impv. ava тАШhelpтАЩ in the next p─Бda.

In the last p─Бda Indra is urged to eat the roasted grains (addhi dh─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е). The same grains are prepared for the horses to eat in vs. 7: it seems somewhat surprising that Indra and his horses receive the same fodder, as it were – though calling the horses IndraтАЩs тАЬcomrades in joint revelryтАЭ in the next vs. (4b) suggests that they consume the offered meal together. I also don’t understand why the grains should be тАЬof the same appearance every day.тАЭ This phrase is essentially repeated in III.52.8, which also contains 5 occurrences of dh─Бn─Б- (or deriv.). Perhaps the point is that we unfailingly make the same offering to Indra daily; he neednтАЩt worry that we will substitute inferior food.

Griffith

Bring the strong Steeds who drink the warm libation, and, Bull of Godlike nature, be thou gracious.
Let thy Steeds eat; set free thy Tawny Horses, and roasted grain like this consume thou daily.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI harness with prayer your horses, who are to be harnessed with prayer, who are allies and swift-paced in battle; arise, and all-knowing Indra, mounting on your firm and easy chariot, come to the libation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With a sacred formulation I yoke for you the formulation-yoked pair of fallow bays, your swift comrades in joint revelry.
O Indra, mounting the sturdy, well-naved chariot, thinking ahead,
knowing, drive up to the soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The double etymological figure in p─Бda a is almost awkwardly heavy: br├бhmaс╣З─Б te brahmay├║j─Б yunajmi, an awkwardness necessarily reflected in the tr.

Griffith

Those who are yoked by prayer I harness, fleet friendly Bays who take their joy together.
Mounting thy firm and easy car, O Indra, wise and all-knowing come thou to the Soma.

Geldner

Mit kr├дftigem Zuspruch schirre ich dir die beiden durch blo├Яen Zuspruch geschirrten Falben, deine Kameraden bei dem Somagelage, die Renner. Besteige den festen, leichten Wagen, o Indra, und komm des Weges kundig als Kenner zum Soma!

Grassmann

Ich schirre dir durch Spruch die spruchgeschirrten das rasche Rossepaar beim Mahl, o Indra, Besteig den festen gutgeschmierten Wagen, des Weges kundig, komme her zum Soma.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬLet not other sacrifices attract your vigorous and smooth-backed steeds; disregarding others, come perpetually hither, that we may propitiate you sufficiently with effused Soma libations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let other sacrificers not stop your bullish, straight-backed fallow bays. Drive beyond them, each and every one. We will prepare properly for you with pressed soma drinks.

Griffith

No other worshippers must stay beside them thy Bays, thy vigorous and smooth-backed Coursers.
Pass by them all and hasten onward hither: with Soma pressed we will prepare to feast thee.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis soma libation is for you; come down, and well disposed, drink of it unceasingly; seated on the grass at this sacrifice, take Indra, this (libation) into your belly.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 26.23

Jamison Brereton

Yours is this soma here. Come here, nearby. Well-disposed, drink of it each time anew.
At just this sacrifice, having sat down on the ritual grass, put just this drop into your belly, Indra.

Griffith

Thine is this Sorna: hasten to approach it. Drink thou thereof, benevolent, and cease not.
Sit on the sacred grass at this our worship, and take these drops into thy belly, Indra.

Geldner

F├╝r dich ist dieser Soma, komm heran, zum soundsovielten Male trink wohlgemut von diesem! Setz dich zu diesem Opfer auf das Barhis und nimm den Saft in deinem Bauch auf, Indra!

Grassmann

Der Soma hier ist dein, o komme nah her, mit lust’gem Sinne trinke fort und fort ihn; Bei diesem Opfer sitzend auf der Streu hier nimm diesen Indu, Indra, in den Bauch auf.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рддрд╡ рдпреЛрд╜рдпрдорд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЩреН рд╕реЛрдорд╕реНрддрдВ рд╢рд╢реНрд╡рддреНрддрдордВ рддреНрд╡рдореЗрд╣рд┐ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╖рд┐ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рдирд┐рд╖рджреНрдп рд╕реБрдордирд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрдирд┐рдордВ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐ред рдЕрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдорд┐рдиреНрджреБрдВ рдЬрдард░ рдЖ рджрдзрд┐рд╖реНрд╡ рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

English translation:

тАЬThe sacred grass is strewn for you; the Soma, Indra, is poured forth; the grain wherewith to feed your horses is prepared; the oblations are offered to you abiding on the sacred grass, who is praised of many, and is the showerer (of benefits), attended by the Maruts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The ritual grass has been strewn for you, the soma pressed, o Indra. The roasted grains have been prepared for your fallow bays to eat.
To the bull of many talents who is accustomed to it, to you
accompanied by the Maruts are the oblations given.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All the clauses in this vs. are nominal sentences with past participle as predicate (st─лrс╣З├бm, sut├бс╕е a, kс╣Ыt─Б╠Бс╕е b, r─Бt─Б╠Бс╕е d). It is therefore misleading to tr. the last as тАЬare givenтАЭ (versus тАЬhas been strewn,тАЭ etc.) as in the published translation I would change to тАЬhave been given.тАЭ

Griffith

The grass is strewn for thee, pressed is the Soma; the grain is ready for thy Bays to feed on.
To thee who lovest them, the very mighty, strong, girt by Maruts, are these gifts presented.

Geldner

Das Barhis ist f├╝r dich ausgelegt, der Soma ist gepre├Яt, o Indra, die Gerstenk├╢rner sind f├╝r deine Falben zum Essen bereitet. Wie du es gewohnt bist, sind dir, dem vielverm├╢genden Bullen in Begleitung der Marut die Opfergaben gespendet.

Grassmann

Gestreut ist Streu, gepresst der Soma, Indra, gekocht der Brei zur Speise deinen F├╝chsen; Dir, der es w├╝nscht, dem kraftbegabten Stiere, Marut-umscharten sind gereicht die Speisen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe leaders (of the ceremony) have prepared for you, Indra, this (libation), sweetened with milk, the stones, the water; beautiful Indra, who is favourably disposed, and who is wise, knowing well (the worship) that is according to your peculiar paths, come and drink of this libation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Knowing well the worship: praj─Бnan pathy─Б anu sv─Бс╕е = righty apprehending the praises which are due or peculiar, and which are offered with the rites enjoined by the Vedas.

Jamison Brereton

This (soma) have the men, the mountains, and the waters jointly with the cows made honeyed for you.
Having come here along your own paths, well-disposed, drink of it,
lofty one, thinking ahead, knowing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

praj─Бn├бn vidv─Б╠Бn repeats 4d. The particular relevance of this phrase in either vs. isnтАЩt clear to me.

Griffith

This the sweet draught, with cows, the men, the mountains, the waters, Indra, have for thee made ready.
Come, drink thereof, Sublime One, friendly-minded, foreseeing, knowing well the ways thou goest.

Geldner

Diesen Soma haben die M├дnner, die Berge, die Wasser zusammen mit den K├╝hen f├╝r dich, Indra, zu einem s├╝├Яen Trank bereitet. Komm, du Recke, und trinke wohlgemut davon, wegekundig, deine gewohnten Stra├Яen kennend!

Grassmann

Den s├╝ssen Trank hier machten dir die M├дnner, die Steine, Wasser, Indra, sammt den K├╝hen; O komm und trink ihn wohlgemuth, erbab’ner, der du Bescheid weisst, kennend deine Pfade.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAssociated, Indra, with those Maruts with whom you have shared in the libation, who encouraged you (in battle), and are your attendant troop, drink, desirous of the Soma, along with them, with the tongue of Agni.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The Maruts to whom you gave a share in soma, who strengthened you and became your flockтАФ
joined in pleasure with them, eagerly desirous, drink the soma with the tongue of Agni, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

K├╝mmel (477-80) discusses the stem v─Бva┼Ы- at length, rejecting the usual connection with тИЪva┼Ы тАШdesire, wantтАЩ and assigning it instead to тИЪv─Б┼Ы тАШbellowтАЩ. (Witzel Got┼Н follow this interpr. in our passage; Lubotsky still assigns this form to тИЪva┼Ы.) K├╝mmelтАЩs morphological arguments – lack of u-redupl. and of root ablaut – are strong.

However, although I would concede that the form was derivationally original only to тИЪv─Б┼Ы, I would argue that once a stem v─Бva┼Ы-, built to тИЪv─Б┼Ы тАШbellowтАЩ, became established, it was available to тАЬmigrateтАЭ to тИЪva┼Ы тАШdesireтАЩ, especially because the shortening of the root syllable in this metrically driven formation makes the form look more like тИЪva┼Ы than тИЪv─Б┼Ы. Although the meanings of the two roots might seem so far apart that it would be hard to confuse one for the other, in fact the usual context of тИЪv─Б┼Ы forms narrows the semantic gap considerably: cattle bellow because they want something. K├╝mmel allows for the possibility of semantic overlap as well.

Griffith

The Maruts, they with whom thou sharedst Soma, Indra, who made thee strong and were thine army,-
With these accordant, eagerly desirous drink thou this Soma with the tongue of Agni.

Geldner

Die Marut, die du am Soma teilnehmen lie├Яest, o Indra, die dich st├дrkten und dein Gefolge wurden, mit denen zusammen trinke verlangend durch die Zunge des Agni diesen Soma, Indra!

Grassmann

Mit denen, Indra, du den Soma theiltest, die dich erfreuten, deine Marutscharen, Mit denen trink vereinigt diesen Soma, o Indra lustig mit des Agni Zunge.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAdorable Indra, drink of the effused libation, either by your own effort, or through the tongue of Agni; drink it, ┼Ъakra, offered by the hand of the adhvaryu, or accept the presentation of the oblation (from the hand) of the Hot─Б.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra, drink of the pressed (soma) just by your own power or take a drink with the tongue of Agni, o you who deserve the sacrifice.
Either from the hand of the Adhvaryu or from the oblation of the
Hotar enjoy the offered sacrifice, able one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The occurrence of 2nd sg. act. pres. impv. p├нba and aor. impv. p─Бhi, both to тИЪp─Б тАШdrinkтАЩ, in a disjunctive v─Б construction should give us a good opportunity to discern the functional distinction between the imperatives to these two tense-aspect stems, esp. since, as far as I can see, both imperatives would fit either of the metrical slots occupied. I have in fact tr. as if there is a functional difference: тАШdrinkтАЩ versus тАШtake a drinkтАЩ, but I am not at all convinced that this is correct. Cf. the disc. of the positional tendencies of p├нba ad III.32.1 and note that the same p─Бda opening ├нndra p├нba is found in the next hymn, III.36.2d. However, the same sequence of pres. and aor. to тИЪp─Б is found in III.36.3, so it may well be meaningful. (The standard tr.

render p├нba and p─Бhi identically here.) I take pr├бyatam in c with yaj├▒├бm in d, contra the standard tr.

Griffith

Drink, Indra, of the juice by thine own nature, or by the tongue of Agni, O thou Holy.
Accept the sacrificial gift, O Sakra, from the Adhvaryu’s hand or from the Hotar’s.

Geldner

Indra! Trink nach eignem Ermessen vom Soma oder trink mit der Zunge des Agni, du Opferw├╝rdiger, oder aus der Hand des Adhvaryu den dargebotenen, du M├дchtiger, oder erfreue dich an dem Weihspruch des Hotri zur Opferspende!

Grassmann

O Indra, trink auf eigne Hand vom Safte, o hehrer, oder mit des Agni Zunge; Geniess, o Starker, das gereichte Opfer aus Dieners Hand und aus dem Guss des Priesters.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рдпрдореВрддрдпреЗ рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЗрд╡ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдореБрдЧреНрд░рдВ рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдЮреНрдЬрд┐рддрдорд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрднрд░реЗ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ рдиреГрддрдордВ рд╢реБрдирдВ рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рд╣реБрд╡реЗрдо рддрдерд╛рд╜рдкреНрдпреЗрддрдВ рдпреВрдпрдордкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдд реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╢реБрдирдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд░рдореН (рд╣реБрд╡реЗрдо) (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдореН) рдмрд╣реБрдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЗ (рднрд░реЗ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рдиреГрддрдордореН) рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрддреНрддрдордореН (рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ) рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧреЗ (рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН) рд╕рддреНрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╢реНрд░реЛрддрд╛рд░рдореН (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдореН) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдореН (рдКрддрдпреЗ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдп (рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ (рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдореН) рдирд╛рд╢рдпрдиреНрддрдореН (рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреНрдмрд▓рд╛рд╜рд╜рд╡рд░рдХрд╛рдгрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕реИрдиреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╕рдЮреНрдЬрд┐рддрдореН) (рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдореН реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдирд┐рд╖реНрдлрд▓рдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рдирд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдиреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╡реГрдгреБрддреЗрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрдиреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдВ рддреБрд░рдЩреНрдЧрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддреЗрдиреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╖реНрдЯрд╛рджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреЛ! рдЬреНрдпрд╛ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рдХрд░реНрдо рдирд┐рд╖реНрдлрд▓ рдирд╛рд╣реА, рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдареА рддреБрдореНрд╣реА рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рд╛. рее резрез рее
